  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e61d8a80-d82c-4060-a917-b9179c9b6cf6'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer13694960772275844307">A cursed girl escapes death and finds herself in a magical world - but is then tested beyond her wildest imagination<br/><br/>Morrigan Crow is cursed. Having been born on Eventide, the unluckiest day for any child to be born, she's blamed for all local misfortunes, from hailstorms to heart attacks--and, worst of all, the curse means that Morrigan is doomed to die at midnight on her </span>
  <span id="freeText13694960772275844307" style="display:none">A cursed girl escapes death and finds herself in a magical world - but is then tested beyond her wildest imagination<br /><br />Morrigan Crow is cursed. Having been born on Eventide, the unluckiest day for any child to be born, she's blamed for all local misfortunes, from hailstorms to heart attacks--and, worst of all, the curse means that Morrigan is doomed to die at midnight on her eleventh birthday.<br /><br />But as Morrigan awaits her fate, a strange and remarkable man named Jupiter North appears. Chased by black-smoke hounds and shadowy hunters on horseback, he whisks her away into the safety of a secret, magical city called Nevermoor.<br /><br />It's then that Morrigan discovers Jupiter has chosen her to contend for a place in the city's most prestigious organization: the Wundrous Society. In order to join, she must compete in four difficult and dangerous trials against hundreds of other children, each boasting an extraordinary talent that sets them apart - an extraordinary talent that Morrigan insists she does not have. To stay in the safety of Nevermoor for good, Morrigan will need to find a way to pass the tests - or she'll have to leave the city to confront her deadly fate.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13694960772275844307" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });
      $('span_class_gr-hyperlink_sort_order_span_tip_62').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>    </div>
</div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2480792968?book_show_action=true">Aug 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Giordano" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Giordano" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano">Emma Giordano</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30604861-emma-giordano?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2480792968" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7494087275384008736">This book is absolutely enchanting. <i>Nevermoor</i> is an exciting fantasy tale full of magic, mischief, and wonder. I cannot recommend it enough!<br/><br/><i>Nevermoor</i> is by far the ONLY book I have read that comes close to bringing me the feelings I have while reading <i>Harry Potter</i>. It remains creative and unique while instilling the same emotions, excitement (and fear) of one of the greatest children’s novels of all time. That being said, <i>Nevermoor</i> truly stands on it’s own as a spectacular middle grade adventure</span>
  <span id="freeText7494087275384008736" style="display:none">This book is absolutely enchanting. <i>Nevermoor</i> is an exciting fantasy tale full of magic, mischief, and wonder. I cannot recommend it enough!<br /><br /><i>Nevermoor</i> is by far the ONLY book I have read that comes close to bringing me the feelings I have while reading <i>Harry Potter</i>. It remains creative and unique while instilling the same emotions, excitement (and fear) of one of the greatest children’s novels of all time. That being said, <i>Nevermoor</i> truly stands on it’s own as a spectacular middle grade adventure that will leave you craving more every time you set the book down.<br /><br />This is the perfect tale of sweet and thrilling. It features a high stakes competition that will keep you on the edge of your seat at every trial, while also focusing on the importance of friendship and believing in yourself. Morrigan is such a fantastic protagonist with endless complexities and loveable traits. It is a charming, developed world with a unique magic system and fascinating characters. There are so many twists and turns and unanticipated events that it’s hard not to love.<br /><br />Additionally, the audiobook is PHENOMENAL. If you are an audiobook listener, you MUST consume this story in that format. Gemma Whelan takes this story to new heights with unique character voices, fantastic acting, and flawless execution. There’s also these whimsical little jingles that signal the end of the chapter which was a really nice touch. This novel has absolutely become one of my favorite audiobooks of all time.<br /><br />My only small critique of the book is that I felt the chapters ended at odd times. Sometimes it felt as if it would stop mid-conversation/mid-scene and there were better breaking points a page or two into the next chapter. It was a slight distraction at some points but did not impact my overall enjoyment of the story.<br /><br /><i>Nevermoor</i> has truly stolen my heart. I’m irrevocably in love with this series from the first installment and am anxiously awaiting the sequel. I would highly recommend to any reader of any age. This is a whimsical tale you will not want to miss.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2291371735" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2291371735" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2291371735?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2291371735" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12871979018510910086"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1521063917i/25214563._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“The point is—as far as the Society is concerned—if you are not honest, and determined, and brave, then it doesn’t matter how talented you are.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>Whenever people compare things to <i>Harry Potter</i> I immediately become wary of whatever they are comparing to it. I know this mostly comes from nostalgia, but still, I feel like saying something is “the next <i>Harry Potter</i>” is not only the highest praise, but also setting that thing up for the greatest fall. It took me a while to pick <i>Nevermoor: T</i></span>
  <span id="freeText12871979018510910086" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1521063917i/25214563._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“The point is—as far as the Society is concerned—if you are not honest, and determined, and brave, then it doesn’t matter how talented you are.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Whenever people compare things to <i>Harry Potter</i> I immediately become wary of whatever they are comparing to it. I know this mostly comes from nostalgia, but still, I feel like saying something is “the next <i>Harry Potter</i>” is not only the highest praise, but also setting that thing up for the greatest fall. It took me a while to pick <i>Nevermoor: The Trials of Morrigan Crow</i> up, just because of that that. But you know what? I think it deserves that title; not only is it amazing, it actually does feel like the closest thing I’ve ever read to <i>Harry Potter</i>, while also completely and wholeheartedly being its own story. I loved this book.<br><br>This book stars a young girl named Morrigan Crow, who has lived her life feeling unwanted by a family who believes her to be cursed. And this curse has also lead everyone, including Morrigan, to believe that she will die on her eleventh birthday. That is, until Jupiter North comes with an invitation to compete to join the Wundrous Society.<br><br>Each year, kids compete to enter this exclusive Society, with the help of a sponsor. And all the children have different knacks, AKA: talents, which range from being able to grow hair on a whim, to being able to ride dragons, to being practically invisible, the possibilities are honestly endless. And Jupiter North has never taken a protégée under his wing, until Morrigan. So, everyone is wondering and assuming that she must have a talent unlike anyone has ever seen, but Morrigan doesn’t even know what special powers she possesses. <br><br>But to even get into the Wundrous Society, Morrigan must complete each of the four trials. And all the trials are so very different, and so very unique, and such a dang treat to read. The trials were truly my favorite scenes in this book. And that’s saying a lot, because we have a giant, talking cat who is sassy and perfect. And a hotel, where Morrigan stays, with such an amazing cast of characters. And the Christmas scene and competition in this book? Honestly perfection. I truly did love this story with my whole heart. <br><br>This book is such a love letter to found families. And I think this book could change so many lives of so many kids out there that feel so unwanted, when in reality they are so very wanted and the family we choose will always be greater than the family we are born into. This is something that took me a long while to figure out myself, but blood will always be just that – blood. Hell, every one out of fifteen people walking around Vegas are likely to have my blood type, and that’s all my blood has to say about me. Yes, this book is whimsical, and fun, but I also think it’s important. And my heart is so very happy just thinking about the message that will touch so many kids picking this book up. <br><br>And this book has such an overwhelming message about how we can truly be anything we want to be. That good and bad are in all of us, and as long as you’re striving to do good, you can be good, no matter your past, and no matter who tells you otherwise. <br><br>Overall, I can honestly say that each time I opened this book up that I experienced pure joy. From the messages, to the writing, to this fantastic story in general. There is so much to love about this book. If you are on the fence, please pick this one up. It’s honestly such a bright shining light in middle grade. And I cannot wait to see what comes next in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2468232586" rel="nofollow noopener">Wundersmith: The Calling of Morrigan Crow</a>! <br><br><a <div id="review_2065005240" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2065005240" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2065005240?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=competition">competition</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2065005240" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14603180128717783061">4 1/2 stars. This could be the beginning of a new series phenomenon. What do you say, Jessica Townsend? Are you ready for it?<br/><br/>Morrigan Crow was born to die on her eleventh birthday. She is cursed. But an invitation to the elusive Wundrous Society changes her destiny. <br/><br/>She needs to pass challenging trials that will determine if she has it in her to be part of something bigger than herself and join the elite group. <br/><br/>But everyone seems to have a talent, something that makes them… magical. Except her. </span>
  <span id="freeText14603180128717783061" style="display:none">4 1/2 stars. This could be the beginning of a new series phenomenon. What do you say, Jessica Townsend? Are you ready for it?<br /><br />Morrigan Crow was born to die on her eleventh birthday. She is cursed. But an invitation to the elusive Wundrous Society changes her destiny. <br /><br />She needs to pass challenging trials that will determine if she has it in her to be part of something bigger than herself and join the elite group. <br /><br />But everyone seems to have a talent, something that makes them… magical. Except her. Will she find it before it’s too late? Either she becomes part of the secret organization, or she dies. <br /><br />Jessica Townsend knows what readers want. She knows we need to be hooked and surprised and mystified. Being hooked is easy, as the world building is special, like a cake with multiple layers. You think you’ve tasted it all, only to discover there are more hidden flavours.<br /><br />I’m one for competitions, so the trials had me going. They are extremely concealed, until it’s the right time to disclose what the children will need to do. Having read the book, I can tell you they are not predictable, hence the surprising factor. <br /><br />As with any book, if we already know everything, there is little use to keeping on reading. The characters have secrets. The Wundrous Society itself is a mystery. Even now, I feel as if I’ve only been privy to 5% of its mysteries, at most. I don’t know if it’s a sort of school or spy society…<br /><br />It’s killing me, of course, but it’s also making me die to pick the sequel up, which is the ideal reaction after finishing a book. Jessica Townsend did that to me. It’s when you’re ready to cry at the idea of a book not having any sequels that you know it made its mark on you. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14603180128717783061" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2493268295" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer139258004036683572"><b>Middle of the road middle grade.</b><br/><br/>That best describes this reading experience for me, which was a huge bummer. <br/><br/>Someone I follow gushed about this book and how "magical" it was...and it just didn't live up to those expectations for me, sadly.<br/><br/>In fact, this read like a book that was trying too hard to be the next big movie franchise. A lot of the elements of the book felt very choppy and very clearly borrowed from other huge blockbusters, i.e., <i>Harry Potter</i> (obviously), <i>The Hunger Games</i>, <i>Mary Poppins</i></span>
  <span id="freeText139258004036683572" style="display:none"><b>Middle of the road middle grade.</b><br /><br />That best describes this reading experience for me, which was a huge bummer. <br /><br />Someone I follow gushed about this book and how "magical" it was...and it just didn't live up to those expectations for me, sadly.<br /><br />In fact, this read like a book that was trying too hard to be the next big movie franchise. A lot of the elements of the book felt very choppy and very clearly borrowed from other huge blockbusters, i.e., <i>Harry Potter</i> (obviously), <i>The Hunger Games</i>, <i>Mary Poppins</i> and <i>The Wizard of Oz</i>, to name just a few. <br /><br />Full disclosure, though: the fact that I read this on the heels of my FIRST read of <i>Harry Potter and the Prizoner of Azkaban</i> (my first read of the HP series ever in general) probably didn't help matters any. <br /><br />All that said, while the story didn't blow me away, I DID enjoy it well enough. The main character, Morrigan, read pretty flat for me this go-round; but, I really liked Jupiter North and Hawthorne Swift and I will still read the next one to find out what happens. <br /><br />And who knows, maybe I will like this better upon a second read when I'm prepping for book two.</span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2661290366" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer8506009196746601929"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1551534793i/27143282._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b> My thoughts in a nutshell </b><br/>Awww! This was so adorable. I don't really enjoy middle-grade category because I always feel too old myself for that, but I didn't feel it with Nevermoor. <b>Everyone compares this book to Harry Potter. Nevermoor is not Harry Potter. They have nothing to do with each other. Keep in mind!</b><br/><br/><b>The story is about…</b><br/><u>Skip over this point if you don't like the sneak peek. </u><br/>Morrigan, who is a "cursed" child. She travels to Nevermoor and she has to do four trials to become a member of Wu</span>
  <span id="freeText8506009196746601929" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1551534793i/27143282._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b> My thoughts in a nutshell </b><br>Awww! This was so adorable. I don't really enjoy middle-grade category because I always feel too old myself for that, but I didn't feel it with Nevermoor. <b>Everyone compares this book to Harry Potter. Nevermoor is not Harry Potter. They have nothing to do with each other. Keep in mind!</b><br><br><b>The story is about…</b><br><u>Skip over this point if you don't like the sneak peek. </u><br>Morrigan, who is a "cursed" child. She travels to Nevermoor and she has to do four trials to become a member of Wundrous Society.<br><br><b> What impressed me </b><br>Nevermoor is such a fascinating and imaginative read. I adored the whole world-building, it was so magical and whimsical. <br>If something terrible happened, society blamed Morrigan because she is a cursed girl. So, the book started with Morrigan's apologies letters. I laughed so much about that. <br>I loved the characterization of this novel. Every character has a personality even though it is a middle-grade book! <br>Morrigan is a brave, intelligent little girl. I liked her temperament. She is an excellent protagonist.<br>I don't know why, but I thought through the book that Jupiter is a woman. I saw that he is a gentleman, but my brain kept telling me he is a she. LOL. It makes no sense, I know. <br>Anyway, he was my absolute favorite person. His attitude and humor worked for me perfectly.<br>I enjoyed the trials. All were interesting and exciting, but my favorite was the first one, the talking paper. I want the same exam method at my school.<br>Nevermoor's most powerful point is the writing style. Jessica Townsend is a talented storyteller. I admire how fluent and fabulous her book is. <br>The ending was predictable, but I still enjoy it. I will probably read the second and third book.<br><b>I listened to the audiobook version, the narrator did a fantastic job. Her voice brought the story to life.</b><br><br><b>What I don't like </b><br>It was a bit long. I felt some part was over-written and I noticed I started to feel some boredom. This is just a personal opinion. I'm starting to get bored soon if the book is too repetitive.<br><br><b> Make a conclusion </b><br>Overall, Nevermoor is a real page-turner. <b>I highly recommend it to young and adult as well. It is an utterly delightful and lighthearted read for the summer. </b> I gave it a strong 4 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8506009196746601929" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2189907638365067231">Actual rating: 4,5 stars<br/><br/>This was really good!<br/>If you ask me, all the hype this book got was totally justified.<br/><br/>The novel is often compared to Harry Potter and I can see why (young chosen protagonist, villain who's name people are afraid to say out loud, magic), but still, those are two very different stories.<br/><br/>It's rare when book compels me from the prologue, and that was what happened with Nevermoor.<br/><br/>I lost myself in this magical world, but if I'm being honest, at times I was also lost.<br/>I ascribe tha</span>
  <span id="freeText2189907638365067231" style="display:none">Actual rating: 4,5 stars<br /><br />This was really good!<br />If you ask me, all the hype this book got was totally justified.<br /><br />The novel is often compared to Harry Potter and I can see why (young chosen protagonist, villain who's name people are afraid to say out loud, magic), but still, those are two very different stories.<br /><br />It's rare when book compels me from the prologue, and that was what happened with Nevermoor.<br /><br />I lost myself in this magical world, but if I'm being honest, at times I was also lost.<br />I ascribe that to the fact that English is not my first language, and I am still exploring fantasy. Since this is aimed to middle graders, I think it will be easy to follow to most readers, if not everyone.<br /><br />I loved Morrigan as a main character, but I also enjoyed reading about all of her friends.<br />My favourite was Fenestra, the giant cat, and I wish I could have one for myself. <br />If only one of my cats could became a magical creature similar to her (but not GiGi because he would be dangerous!).<br /><br />I loved The Trials of Morrigan Crow so much that I plan to visit a bookstore by the end of this week to buy myself a sequel!<br /><br />I highly recommend this one to all middle graders and adults who enjoyed Harry Potter, but want to read something original.</span>

<div id="review_1882428662" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1882428662" />
    <a title="Carolyn  K." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19831039-carolyn-k"><img alt="Carolyn  K." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1398886831p2/19831039.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1882428662?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carolyn  K." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carolyn  K." href="/user/show/19831039-carolyn-k">Carolyn  K.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/33276673-nevermoor">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1882428662" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3676926328130996082">What in the world... <br/><br/>Jessica Townsend's Nevermoor: The Trials of Morrigan Crow had garnered an exceeding amount of praise and recognition throughout news articles, catching my attention as well. From the film rights already sold to a 7-figure deal between major publishers and even being likened to Harry Potter (I mean no I didn't buy it of course, but c'mon don't we readers all get hopeful that the next big thing is finally here?) Nevermoor ignited so much buzz on the web that I had to see for m</span>
  <span id="freeText3676926328130996082" style="display:none">What in the world... <br /><br />Jessica Townsend's Nevermoor: The Trials of Morrigan Crow had garnered an exceeding amount of praise and recognition throughout news articles, catching my attention as well. From the film rights already sold to a 7-figure deal between major publishers and even being likened to Harry Potter (I mean no I didn't buy it of course, but c'mon don't we readers all get hopeful that the next big thing is finally here?) Nevermoor ignited so much buzz on the web that I had to see for myself if this novel was worth the hype. <br /><br />Most unfortunately, it wasn't. Not even close to it. <br /><br />How to describe Nevermoor? A mash-up of Mary Poppins, Harry Potter, and Hotel Transylvania. I use the Harry Potter card carefully. It is not thrilling, sophisticated, and creative as Harry Potter. I say Harry Potter only because there were similar aspects like how Morrigan is a "cursed child" and grows up being very lonely and feared/hated by others. And there are plenty of other scenes that are reminiscent of Harry Potter, which isn't a bad thing, but only is if it feels redundant and unoriginal. Now, I say Marry Poppins because Jupiter North is Marry Poppins much in masculine form. Period. And lastly, I say Hotel Transylvania because Halloweenish characters appear throughout the novel. <br /><br />I cannot express enough how utterly disappointed I am. Nevermoor did not wow me, amaze me, entertain me, impress me, or even amuse me. It did not do the very thing news articles, Goodreads reviewers, and blurbs relentlessly promised: to wow me and us readers. It was a long, jarring flop. <br /><br />Morrigan Crow was one dimensional. She always feels like the background, experiencing everything from afar and not keen to make her own decisions nor ask questions when she needs to. She's not independent nor strong-minded. Jupiter North once again is Mary Poppins. Eccentric, warm hearted, and a mentor to Morrigan. Now, the story lacks conflict and tension. And I've seen and loved plenty of children's novels that have those essential aspects. So the whole book from beginning to end felt like a long, exhausting, and taxing read. It literally drained the energy out of me. <br /><br />The writing wasn't anything special. I believe the writer doesn't know how to write figuratively. It was extremely dry, plain and unoriginal. It didn't help that the main character was almost always in a drab and gloomy mood. Another issue about this book is that the relative location of the characters in a scene isn't described thoroughly. For example, there was a scene where Morrigan went into the elevator with Jupiter, but all of a sudden there were a bunch of people with them and Martha the maid was there. And this happened consistently. Or supporting characters were not described very thoroughly in detail like their physical appearance and personalities. And they felt like placeholders, not unique or charming in any way. It was sometimes very frustrating. <br /><br />Another biggie problem was how the conflicts were solved. Goodness! Trial after trial, Morrigan smoothly passed through all including the climax of the novel by slim needle hole of luck that she'll easily pass through. It was strange and upsetting. None of it felt believable. It didn't support or enrich Morrigan's character. Because she slipped through so easy in all of these "daring and difficult" trials and other conflicts, the conflicts didn't feel like conflicts at all. <br /><br />Overall, this novel did not meet up with all the hype. It's actually really mediocre. I still cannot understand how so much praise was given to this novel. There wasn't a deep meaning or theme within the book that could outshine the slow paced, dull plot. This is just a typical children's novel that is easily forgotten. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3676926328130996082" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2242938698" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4561327131522001717"><b>Oh my! That was *Magnificat! I mean Magnificent! </b><br/><br/>I realize that the below quote is quite long... But it sets the tone of this fantastic book! Enjoy! <br/><br/><i>Jupiter was gazing anxiously out the window now, a frown creasing his forehead. “You did actually sign the contract before you burned it, though,” he said without looking at her. “And who says you’re going to die? You don’t have to die if you don’t want to.”<br/> Corvus slammed his fist on the table. “This is intolerable! Who do you think you are, waltzi</i></span>
  <span id="freeText4561327131522001717" style="display:none"><b>Oh my! That was *Magnificat! I mean Magnificent! </b><br /><br />I realize that the below quote is quite long... But it sets the tone of this fantastic book! Enjoy! <br /><br /><i>Jupiter was gazing anxiously out the window now, a frown creasing his forehead. “You did actually sign the contract before you burned it, though,” he said without looking at her. “And who says you’re going to die? You don’t have to die if you don’t want to.”<br /> Corvus slammed his fist on the table. “This is intolerable! Who do you think you are, waltzing into my home and upsetting my family with this nonsense?” <br />“I told you who I am.” Jupiter spoke patiently, as if to a senseless child. “My name is Jupiter North.” <br />“And I am Corvus Crow, the state chancellor of Great Wolfacre and a ranked member of the Wintersea Party,” said Corvus, puffing up his chest. He was on a roll now. “I demand that you go at once, and allow me to mourn the death of my daughter in peace.” <br />“Mourn the death of your daughter?” echoed Jupiter. He took two deliberate steps toward Corvus and paused, his eyes glittering. The hairs on Morrigan’s arms stood up. Jupiter’s voice dropped an entire octave, and he spoke with a cold, quiet anger that was terrible to behold. “Can you possibly mean the daughter standing right in front of you? The one who is demonstrably, superbly, brilliantly alive?” <br />Corvus sputtered and pointed to the clock on the wall, his hand shaking with outrage. “Well, give it a few hours!” <br />Morrigan felt something squeeze in her chest, and she wasn’t sure why. She’d always known she was going to die on Eventide. Her father and grandmother had never kept it secret. It shouldn’t have been a surprise that Corvus was so resigned to her fate, but Morrigan suddenly realized that to him, she might as well be dead already. Perhaps in his heart she’d been dead for years. <br />“Morrigan,” said Jupiter, in a voice very different from the one he’d just used on her father, “don’t you want to live?”<br /> Morrigan flinched. What sort of a question was that? “It doesn’t matter what I want.”<br /> “It does,” he insisted. “It matters so very, very much. Right now it’s the only thing that matters.”<br /> Her eyes flicked from her father to her grandmother to her stepmother. They all watched her intently, uneasily, as if seeing her properly for the first time. “Of course I want to live,” she said quietly. It was the first time she’d ever spoken the words aloud. The tightness in her chest eased a little.<br /> “Good choice.” Jupiter smiled; the cloud disappeared from his face as quickly as it had arrived. He turned back to the window. “Death is boring. Life is much more fun. Things happen in life all the time. Unexpected things. Things you couldn’t possibly expect because they’re so very… unexpected.”<br /> He stepped backward, inching away from the window and reaching blindly for Morrigan, fumbling to take her hand. “For instance, I bet you didn’t expect your so-called death to arrive three hours early.” <br />Morrigan felt something powdery land on her face. Wiping it away, she looked up to see the light fixtures shaking and cracks appearing in the plaster. The lightbulbs stuttered and buzzed. The windows began to rattle. There was a faint smell of burning. <br />“What’s that?” She squeezed his hand automatically. “What’s happening?” <br />Jupiter leaned down to whisper in her ear. “Do you trust me?” <br />She answered without thinking. “Yes.” <br />“You sure?” <br />“Positive.” <br />“All right.” He looked her in the eye. The floor trembled beneath their feet. “I’m going to take that curtain down in a moment. But whatever you see out there, you mustn’t be afraid. They can tell when you’re afraid.” <br />Morrigan swallowed. “They?” <br />“Just follow my lead and you’ll be fine. Yes? No fear.” <br />“No fear,” repeated Morrigan. Meanwhile, fear had set up camp in her stomach and was having a festival. A Ferris wheel of fear spun idly in her abdomen. Dancing circus elephants of fear somersaulted through her intestinal tract. <br />“What the devil are you talking about over there?” said Grandmother. “What’s he saying to you, Morrigan? I demand to—” <br />In a rush of sudden movement Jupiter pulled a handful of silver dust from his pocket and blew it toward Corvus, Ivy, and Grandmother like a cloudy, starry kiss, then leapt up to the window and ripped down the curtain, dropping it in a crumpled, messy pile in the middle of the floor.<br /> He stood back to gaze at his handiwork and shook his head slowly, mournfully. “I am so sorry. How tragic to have lost her so young.” Corvus frowned and blinked, looking unsure. His eyes were glassy. “Tragic?”<br /> “Mmm,” said Jupiter. He threw an arm around Corvus’s shoulders and led him closer to the pile of fabric. “Dear, dear Morrigan. So full of life. So much to share with the world. But taken! Taken too soon.” <br />“Too soon.” Corvus nodded in shell-shocked agreement. “Much too soon.” <br />Jupiter put his other arm around Ivy and drew her into his chest. “You mustn’t blame yourselves. Although you could a bit, if you wanted to.” He winked at Morrigan, who felt a small, hysterical laugh working its way up out of her throat. Did they really believe that curtain was her, lying dead on the floor? She was standing right in front of them! <br />“She looks so small.” Ivy sniffed and drew her sleeve across her nose. “So small and thin.” <br />“Yes,” said Jupiter. “Almost as if she were… made of fabric.” <br />Morrigan snorted, but the Crows made no sign that they’d heard her. <br />“I’ll leave you to make the necessary arrangements. You’ll need to prepare a statement for the press, Chancellor. But before I go, may I suggest a closed casket for the funeral? Open caskets are so tacky.”<br /> “Yes,” said Grandmother, gazing down at curtain-Morrigan. “Indeed. Quite tacky.” <br />“What did you do?” Morrigan whispered to Jupiter. “What was that silver stuff?” <br />“Highly illegal. Pretend you didn’t see it.” <br />The light fixture swung violently, casting shadows across the room. An unmistakable smell of woodsmoke filled the air. The floor began to shake again, and in the distance Morrigan heard something like heavy rain or rolling thunder or—was it—hoofbeats? <br />She turned to the window and felt a hot, prickling fear all the way down her spine. Panic rose like bile in her throat. She could see it. She could see her death coming.</i><br /><br />********<br />The audiobook edition of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34219873.The_Trials_of_Morrigan_Crow__Nevermoor___1_" title="The Trials of Morrigan Crow (Nevermoor, #1) by Jessica Townsend" rel="nofollow noopener">The Trials of Morrigan Crow</a> is a difficult book to put into words as I loved every minute of it. Until it ended that is. 🙁<br />So my review is brief but I think it get right down to the heart of my thoughts. <br /><br />In short, the dynamic combination of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/19251469.Jessica_Townsend" title="Jessica Townsend" rel="nofollow noopener">Jessica Townsend</a>'s unbelievably glorious debut and the phenomenal narrative performance of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4024869.Gemma_Whelan" title="Gemma Whelan" rel="nofollow noopener">Gemma Whelan</a> creates a stunning and absolutely magnificent listen! The story jumps off the pages into living color and tangible reality! <br />The *Magnificat I mentioned is one of my favorite characters! <br /><br />It's a collosal rollercoaster ride full of a range of emotions that will send listeners into hours of exciting entertainment! Loaded with amusing, hilarious, and uplifting fun that made me laugh out loud along with perilous adventures that bring fear, dread, and uncertainty that gave me goosebumps. <br />And, of course, there's the teasing cliffhanger of what will be happen next in Morrigan's future. <br />I loved and adored this audiobook!<br />Do give it a listen! YOU WILL NOT BE DISSAPOINTED!<br /><br /><br />When I listened to this the first two times I read book two, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36260006.Wundersmith_The_Calling_of_Morrigan_Crow__Nevermoor___2_" title="Wundersmith The Calling of Morrigan Crow (Nevermoor, #2) by Jessica Townsend" rel="nofollow noopener">Wundersmith: The Calling of Morrigan Crow</a>, as it wasn't available on audiobook. However, just a few days ago I searched again and discovered that there IS an audiobook edition AVAILABLE NOW! Even more exciting is that it is, once again, performed by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4024869.Gemma_Whelan" title="Gemma Whelan" rel="nofollow noopener">Gemma Whelan</a>! Stay tuned for my review of the second installment! I've already started listening to it even before I wrote this review! And now there will be the release of book three, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/46196106.Hollowpox_The_Hunt_for_Morrigan_Crow" title="Hollowpox The Hunt for Morrigan Crow by Jessica Townsend" rel="nofollow noopener">Hollowpox: The Hunt for Morrigan Crow</a>, in August, 2020. Sadly I can't find an audiobook but I'm not bothered about it as the <i>Nevermoor/Morrigan Crow </i> series is an absolute favorite of mine and I'm excited to read it! <br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2295618365" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8441925646236571214"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34219873.The_Trials_of_Morrigan_Crow__Nevermoor___1_' title='The Trials of Morrigan Crow (Nevermoor, #1) by Jessica Townsend' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Trials of Morrigan Crow</a> is one of those middle grade children's books which is still perfectly readable by adults who like fantasy. I loved it.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16727429.Jessica_Townsend' title='Jessica Townsend' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jessica Townsend</a> introduces her magical world by saying little but showing lots - just the way it should be done. There's a wonderful talking cat and a hotel which creates itself according to the resident's needs and desires. There are dragons and dragon riders. There are witches and people who can perform amazing tasks. And there is much more!<br/><br/>All of </span>
  <span id="freeText8441925646236571214" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34219873.The_Trials_of_Morrigan_Crow__Nevermoor___1_" title="The Trials of Morrigan Crow (Nevermoor, #1) by Jessica Townsend" rel="nofollow noopener">The Trials of Morrigan Crow</a> is one of those middle grade children's books which is still perfectly readable by adults who like fantasy. I loved it.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16727429.Jessica_Townsend" title="Jessica Townsend" rel="nofollow noopener">Jessica Townsend</a> introduces her magical world by saying little but showing lots - just the way it should be done. There's a wonderful talking cat and a hotel which creates itself according to the resident's needs and desires. There are dragons and dragon riders. There are witches and people who can perform amazing tasks. And there is much more!<br /><br />All of the characters are delightful especially Jupiter and Hawthorne. Morrigan Crow herself shows tremendous promise of good things to come in future books. The story is excellent and is complete in this book but with plenty of hints about what is to come.<br /><br />And all of this was well written, nicely paced and thoroughly enjoyable. Five stars for this first episode in the series and I look forward to much more.</span>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2208466515" />

<div id="review_2463602530" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2463602530" />
    <a title="Helene Jeppesen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21992464-helene-jeppesen"><img alt="Helene Jeppesen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528006866p2/21992464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2463602530?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helene Jeppesen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helene Jeppesen" href="/user/show/21992464-helene-jeppesen">Helene Jeppesen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35560263-nevermoor">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2463602530" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10129791024557702164">This is a wonderful story that sends you on a journey, quite like Harry Potter. I think that if I had read this as a child, I would’ve given it 5 stars. But reading it as an adult was very much like reading the first Harry Potter book (and probably also other fantasy children’s books I can’t think of now), which made me able to clearly predict and guess the storyline before it played out. <br/>That being said, this was a wonderful story that contains everything that a children’s book should contain: </span>
  <span id="freeText10129791024557702164" style="display:none">This is a wonderful story that sends you on a journey, quite like Harry Potter. I think that if I had read this as a child, I would’ve given it 5 stars. But reading it as an adult was very much like reading the first Harry Potter book (and probably also other fantasy children’s books I can’t think of now), which made me able to clearly predict and guess the storyline before it played out. <br />That being said, this was a wonderful story that contains everything that a children’s book should contain: Discoveries about yourself, magic, alluring creatures, and friendships contrasted with the ultimate antagonist. There’s especially one scene that made me realize how connected I was to the characters - a scene that made me feel sheer injustice and stomp my feet as a child as I was reading it. <br />This was an alluring start to a series that I’m definitely going to continue reading once the second book comes out in September. Hopefully, that sequel will be less reminiscent of Harry Potter and have more of a plot on its own. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10129791024557702164" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2976895153" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2976895153" />
    <a title="Sara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1170391-sara"><img alt="Sara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590218363p2/1170391.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2976895153?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara" href="/user/show/1170391-sara">Sara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781510103825" href="/book/show/38352645-the-trials-of-morrigan-crow">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=library-loan">library-loan</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=childrens-book">childrens-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2976895153" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16488483831255041220">I LOVED this. It has everything I want in a middle grade book - magic, danger, humour - and a giant grumpy cat called Fenestra.<br/><br/>Morrigan Crow is a cursed child, the blame of every misfortune that happens within her home town. Heart attack? Morrigan’s fault because she asked after your health. Storm destroyed your house? Morrigan’s vault because she stated it was a nice day. Anything and everything considered unlucky is the result of Morrigan. And she’s also destined to die on her eleventh birthda</span>
  <span id="freeText16488483831255041220" style="display:none">I LOVED this. It has everything I want in a middle grade book - magic, danger, humour - and a giant grumpy cat called Fenestra.<br /><br />Morrigan Crow is a cursed child, the blame of every misfortune that happens within her home town. Heart attack? Morrigan’s fault because she asked after your health. Storm destroyed your house? Morrigan’s vault because she stated it was a nice day. Anything and everything considered unlucky is the result of Morrigan. And she’s also destined to die on her eleventh birthday. Worded luck ever. Until at the stroke of midnight on Eventide she’s whisked away by a ginger bearded man called Jupiter North into the magical Free State of Nevermoor. Here, she’s told she’s to be Jupiter’s sponsor to the Wunder Society. A society that accepts a handful of pupils each year. Pupils who are extraordinary. But Morrigan’s nothing but a cursed child. Or so she thinks. <br /><br />I loved Morrigan. Her upbringing as a cursed child has led to her being incredibly self deprecating and full of woe at times, which blends well with the more outgoing personalities she meets in Nevermoor. She lacks confidence and constantly undermines herself, making her instantly endearing and likeable. I could relate to her a lot, and found her multi faceted and complex in nature. Combine this with the mystery surrounding who Morrigan really is, and why Jupiter wants her in Nevermoor, and I was completely invested in her story. <br /><br />The secondary characters are also full fleshed and wonderful. Jupiter North is instantly warm and welcoming to Morrigan, a pillar of friendliness and kindness that Morrigan hasn’t experienced before. Yes, he keep secrets from her which at times I found infuriating, but his reasonings behind it are understandable. The other characters we see in the hotel Deucalion are all a hodgepodge of eclectic, exciting, colourful creations - ranging from a Vampire Dwarf, an opera singer and (my favourite) Fenestra the Magnificat. She’s grumpy, competitive and a previous cage fighter. Never did I realise I needed such a character in my life, but I did. Together they make a wonderful found family, and I loved them all - the hotel itself included, which feels like a character in itself. <br /><br />The writing is wonderful too. It’s full of humour and warmth that lights up the pages and makes the story feel even more magical than it is. There’s mystery and magical trials, adventures, zombies and races, all wrapped up with snippets of history about Nevermoor itself to help sustain and support the readers view of this world. It’s fast paced, but it doesn’t compromise on character development either, building up this wonderful story that hurtles full throttle to the end and a satisfying conclusion that also leaves it open for the series to continue. <br /><br />Honestly, this was the best middle grade book I’ve read this year. If not in the last couple of year. Highly, highly recommend and I can’t wait to read the next one. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16488483831255041220" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8860386930210160439">I enjoyed this book. I liked Morrigan as a character, she’s very charming. As always, there’s a villain and the good, and there are many messages while she’s going through the trials. The writing was quite good. Townsend made the story very exciting, very action packed.   <span id="freeText8860386930210160439" style="display:none">I enjoyed this book. I liked Morrigan as a character, she’s very charming. As always, there’s a villain and the good, and there are many messages while she’s going through the trials. The writing was quite good. Townsend made the story very exciting, very action packed. The world is described in detail that was very enjoyable to read. The side characters were even very well thought through.<br />If you’re going to pick up a middle grade book to enjoy your time and get lost in a magical world with a cute character, it's a good choice. <br />Somehow when I read this first, I was more excited about it. But, as time passed, I realised I didn't care for the sequel that much. So, maybe on reflection, I didn't find it that memorable.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4227558-spencer-orey?shelf=mg-fantasy">mg-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2830067285" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8027668897980620902">This was fun to read! And it built really well toward the next book with a series of exciting mysteries. The world is especially vivid with cool magic.<br/><br/>It's interesting to see the ways that books like this work to build on Harry Potter's legacy while keeping things fresh. For me that also meant that it took a lot of the bad of HP with the good. There's a He-Who-Must-Not-Be-Named, and people are described with negative bodily descriptions that I found mildly offensive. There's even a weird focus o</span>
  <span id="freeText8027668897980620902" style="display:none">This was fun to read! And it built really well toward the next book with a series of exciting mysteries. The world is especially vivid with cool magic.<br /><br />It's interesting to see the ways that books like this work to build on Harry Potter's legacy while keeping things fresh. For me that also meant that it took a lot of the bad of HP with the good. There's a He-Who-Must-Not-Be-Named, and people are described with negative bodily descriptions that I found mildly offensive. There's even a weird focus on Christmas. Trigger warning for surprise Christmas books?<br /><br />The big thing that didn't work for me was how disconnected the characters were from the worlds they come from. First, again like Harry Potter, the main character Morrigan grows up in a horrible family that actively hates her. Except it's worse than that: she lives in a place where everyone believes she's inherently horrible, a little curse on their lives. But she somehow comes out strangely blandly positive despite that. There's almost no sense of trauma or any general sign of her having been affected at all by growing up rich, famous, and despised by society.<br /><br />Related, we get a feeling for how magical these different places are, but there's very little sense of how characters are shaped by those places. It felt to me like a vaguely white Britishy world, dressed up in magic. And the main thing that distinguishes characters in society—besides membership to the super elite exclusive club that kids are all doing trials to join—is the power that they were born with. The strongest powers are so celebrated that even in trials that we're specifically told are meant to establish character, the kids who were simply born powerful are swiftly elevated immediately above those who work hard. That's a dangerous and terrible message to give young readers, and it undermines the wiser things that characters say.<br /><br />Some of those powers are really cool! And some of them are totally inconsistent. There's one character in particular who has a power that makes everyone forget them. To me, that should be a life breaking feature. If nobody can remember you, why would your family remember you? Or, in this case, how would they attract a patron that sponsors them for the actual trials of the book? The power itself is super intriguing but isn't fully followed through. Something like that would create a really shattered person or a psychopath, as far as I can tell. Instead, they're rewarded for being so special and elevated above the others who worked hard.<br /><br />There are great magical creatures too. There's a building or two that seems to be alive. There's a giant magical cat.<br /><br />Anyway, despite my troubles with the conservative worldbuilding, I really did like reading the book. It does a great job of building momentum, and it kept me reading faster and faster! And whatever is going on with "wunder" seems really cool. I'll be reading the next book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8027668897980620902" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2405779537" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2405779537" />
    <a title="HP Saucerer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/80638935-hp-saucerer"><img alt="HP Saucerer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559800724p2/80638935.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2405779537?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="HP Saucerer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="HP Saucerer" href="/user/show/80638935-hp-saucerer">HP Saucerer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316508896" href="/book/show/37946448-nevermoor">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/80638935-hp-saucerer?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/80638935-hp-saucerer?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/80638935-hp-saucerer?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/80638935-hp-saucerer?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/80638935-hp-saucerer?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2405779537" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13273169715556540980"><i>Nevermoor</i> has been making great waves for a while now. Upon its release, came the inevitable comparisons to other commercially successful book series, as did the stories of bidding wars and movie rights, so I was keen to see what all the fuss was about, and having read it, I can confirm that it is truly and utterly brilliant.<br/><br/>Apparently, it took Jessica Townsend almost ten years to write and from very early on it’s evident that this is a book with tremendous scope, a story many years in the makin</span>
  <span id="freeText13273169715556540980" style="display:none"><i>Nevermoor</i> has been making great waves for a while now. Upon its release, came the inevitable comparisons to other commercially successful book series, as did the stories of bidding wars and movie rights, so I was keen to see what all the fuss was about, and having read it, I can confirm that it is truly and utterly brilliant.<br /><br />Apparently, it took Jessica Townsend almost ten years to write and from very early on it’s evident that this is a book with tremendous scope, a story many years in the making, in all of the intricate details included, as well as the great number of exciting plot lines that keep you reading on. We’re not just reading to find out whether Morrigan gets into the <i>Wundrous Society</i>, we’re also reading to discover her <i>knack</i>, to figure out what the inscrutable Mr Jones is up to, to discover what the deal is with Cadence, and why Jack has an eyepatch; there’s just so much going on. Then there’s the complex and colorful array of characters that populate the story: from the loyal and obstinately headstrong Fenestra the Magnificat, to the charismatic and gregarious Jupiter North, to trouble-making dragon-rider Hawthorn, as well as lots of minor characters who more than make their mark; <i>Nevermoor</i> is a truly magical place and somewhere you quickly feel at home. <br /><br />Something which works so well in the book, is the multifaceted world that you can’t help but become immersed in. Not only is it so carefully crafted and detailed, it’s also incredibly alluring. So much so, that you <i>want</i> to stay at the Hotel Deucalion and unwind in the Smoking Parlour. You <i>want</i> to take the Wunderground and travel on the Gossamer Line. You <i>want</i> to visit the Room of Shadows and ride the Brolly Rail. It’s a world absolutely teeming with wonder and the comparisons to <i>Harry Potter</i> and <i>Alice in Wonderland</i>, you have to say, are certainly justified. <br /><br />I enjoyed this book immensely. It’s vivid, imaginative and surprisingly funny. I can’t wait now to read the sequel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13273169715556540980" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10258118415550931905">Born as a cursed girl destined to die on the night of her eleventh birthday, Morrigan Crow was resigned to the fact that it was her fault whenever things went wrong. But as the hours crept toward midnight, Morrigan was rescued – whisked away in an unusual vehicle by a total stranger. Jupiter North was her saviour, and patron, and their arrival in Nevermoor, a magical place which had Morrigan enthralled, felt like a dream.<br/><br/>Hotel Deucalion was to be her home; it was where Jupiter lived – in fact he</span>
  <span id="freeText10258118415550931905" style="display:none">Born as a cursed girl destined to die on the night of her eleventh birthday, Morrigan Crow was resigned to the fact that it was her fault whenever things went wrong. But as the hours crept toward midnight, Morrigan was rescued – whisked away in an unusual vehicle by a total stranger. Jupiter North was her saviour, and patron, and their arrival in Nevermoor, a magical place which had Morrigan enthralled, felt like a dream.<br /><br />Hotel Deucalion was to be her home; it was where Jupiter lived – in fact he owned the charming hotel – and also where the Magnificat, Fenestra resided as head of housekeeping. Fen was a grumpy cat, but she had a heart of gold if one could find it in all that fur. But it was the news that Jupiter expected Morrigan to participate in four tough trials over the coming year, to the end of joining the Wundrous Society, a prestigious and coveted group of people in Nevermoor, that terrified Morrigan. Five hundred children would enter – only nine would be chosen. <br /><br />But though Jupiter told her she was safe in Nevermoor, she wasn’t sure she was. The black-smoke hounds would be baying for her if she failed – her terror was never far from the surface.<br /><br /><i>Nevermoor</i>, first in the Nevermoor series by Aussie author Jessica Townsend is absolutely, breathtakingly brilliant! Fantastical, clever, imaginative, magical – I was riveted, unable to put it down. The author is destined to go a long way in my opinion – and this is her debut! I love the cover – the look on Morrigan’s face as first one, then another leapt from the building with their special umbrella after uttering the words <b>“Step Boldly”</b>. I was thrilled to see book two will be released in 2018! Can’t wait to catch up with Morrigan, Jupiter and the rest of the Nevermoor family! Highly recommended.<br /><br />With thanks to Hachette AU for my copy to read and review.<br /></span>

<div id="review_2557520813" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2557520813" />
    <a title="Kaitlin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin"><img alt="Kaitlin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481663259p2/19126246.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2557520813?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaitlin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaitlin" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin">Kaitlin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2557520813" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14781259887634588125">Yeah, this was brilliantly fun. I see why it's so often compared to Harry Potter, but it's unique in its own right and I really found it a fun story!<br/><br/>This follows Morrigan Crow, a young girl who is cursed and blamed for all of the problems that occur in her town. However, although Morrigan's life up until now hasn't been the best, she is trying to make the most of it because within a year Eventide is due to come and start a new Age and that means she's due to die. <br/><br/>Morrigan was a character I liked</span>
  <span id="freeText14781259887634588125" style="display:none">Yeah, this was brilliantly fun. I see why it's so often compared to Harry Potter, but it's unique in its own right and I really found it a fun story!<br /><br />This follows Morrigan Crow, a young girl who is cursed and blamed for all of the problems that occur in her town. However, although Morrigan's life up until now hasn't been the best, she is trying to make the most of it because within a year Eventide is due to come and start a new Age and that means she's due to die. <br /><br />Morrigan was a character I liked from the start, she's rather sarcastic and silly at times, but she's also very caring and she really does just crave love and trust from those around her. However, when she is faced with the prospect of an early death, she decides that she's rather ready to follow an escape route into another land, Nevermoor, and that's precisely what happens...<br /><br />Nevermoor as a place is fantastical and whimsical and filled with charm and fun. I have to admit that I really liked the ideas that Townsend was playing with here and it felt like a very fresh take on many of the older fantasy tropes. I definitely enjoyed the ideas of Xmas and Halloween (or the Nevermoor versions of them) and the trials were fun to follow to.<br /><br />In general this a perfectly fun story with a lot to enjoy. It felt a little young for me, because it's geared towards children, but it was still a highly enjoyable read and I will be buying the sequel too when it's out. 4*s</span>
  <a data-text-id="14781259887634588125" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2354017765?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ian" href="/user/show/6703235-ian">Ian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6703235-ian?shelf=a-audiobook">a-audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6703235-ian?shelf=t-fairies-trolls-goblins-elves">t-fairies-trolls-goblins-elves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6703235-ian?shelf=t-vampires-werewolves-witches">t-vampires-werewolves-witches</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6703235-ian?shelf=g-young-adult">g-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6703235-ian?shelf=t-cats-lady">t-cats-lady</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2354017765" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15813193683512001529">There is more than just a little of Harry Potter in this book and I still don't quite know what I think about that. <br/><br/>I love the world the author is creating, but those similarities make me uncomfortable. Having said that, <i>The Trials of Morrigan Crow</i> is a debut and I guess debut novels often reflect the author's influences. <br/><br/>And the story really is magical. I believe 20th Century Fox have snapped up the movie rights to it already after only one book.</span>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2694099669" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2694099669" />
    <a title="Meghan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14081543-meghan"><img alt="Meghan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554746625p2/14081543.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2694099669?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meghan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meghan" href="/user/show/14081543-meghan">Meghan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2694099669" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18028143293535443962"><b>**5 OUTSTANDING, WELL-EARNED STARS**</b> . <br/> <br/><b>WOW.</b> I feel speechless. I know I said this before about another book, but this is the best book I have read in 2019 so far. Each book I read this year is better than the last. It has been a long time since I entered a fantasy world as magical, charming, disarming, and unique as <i>The Trials of Morrigan Crow.</i> <br/> <br/>The story follows a cursed young girl destined to die on her eleventh birthday, until she is swept up into Nevermoor, a magical, hidden realm. In Never</span>
  <span id="freeText18028143293535443962" style="display:none"><b>**5 OUTSTANDING, WELL-EARNED STARS**</b> . <br /> <br /><b>WOW.</b> I feel speechless. I know I said this before about another book, but this is the best book I have read in 2019 so far. Each book I read this year is better than the last. It has been a long time since I entered a fantasy world as magical, charming, disarming, and unique as <i>The Trials of Morrigan Crow.</i> <br /> <br />The story follows a cursed young girl destined to die on her eleventh birthday, until she is swept up into Nevermoor, a magical, hidden realm. In Nevermoor, she must complete a set of trials or risk the hunters that are out to kill her. But not all is dark and gloomy. Nevermoor is full of magical, enthralling dwellings and hilarious, quirky characters. The best character of all, I am happy to say, is the main character, Morrigan, who is strong, compassionate, and clever.<br /><br /><i>"Not the best place to study for a test, in Morrigan's opinion, but Fen wouldn't let them eat their lunch in the library and Kedgeree had earlier announced that gravity had been suspended in the dining room until further notice."</i><br /><br />The world that Jessica Townsend creates is truly wondrous. I found myself completely enamored with Nevermoor, the characters, and the magic system. <b>I haven't come across a fantasy story so skillfully detailed and wonderfully unique since Harry Potter. Every detail is important and has a function. Every conversation is intriguing, funny, and informative. Every character is fully fleshed out and has a purpose. <u>There are no wasted words on the page.</u></b><br /><br /><i>"You don't steer, or brake-- and if you kick me in the sides even once, I'll hide raw sardines in your room. You'll never find them, but the stench will seep deep into your skin and clothes and invade your dreams at night until you go mad."</i><br /><br /><i>The Trials of Morrigan Crow</i> is delightfully spooky and equally funny, with a good mix of light and fluffy but also dark humor. I laughed out loud often, and during the most unexpected times, which I found pleasantly surprising. The characters are lovable and wonderfully weird, and you feel yourself become instantly attached to each and every single one. Even the ones that you think are bad. <br /><br />I'll say it again--not a single word, event, conversation, character, detail, ANYTHING, is wasted. Everything is on the page for a reason. The foreshadowing and detail is so excellently done that you KNOW this series is only going to get better as it goes on. Townsend's storytelling reminds me of the level J.K. Rowling is at--that moment in HP when you realized every single little thing mattered and questions left unanswered from the earlier books were eventually answered skillfully and perfectly placed in later books.<br /><br />This is a truly delightful, fun, and consuming story. The amount of skill that went into this is mind-boggling and humbling, and it left me in awe. It is certainly a favorite of mine and I cannot wait to start the second one in the series!</span>
  <a data-text-id="18028143293535443962" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

	<tr>
		<td>
		    <b>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('yDyuBWBqwp+CdpaqdRdNXYsSOf6SvLnlBee0Ksf8XPeQmj5GeYIJsrhsaYG6tgk3sZjioU2jHwxGHSbbZXWUbg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SMEMcF3vMJtksjhF6qpo4fAR15GNCwzOdfT4e2EjNHQQZ5wzRAf7tl6ox24lCyyLypsMzlIUqic2DmqKw6r87Q==')})
  }
//]]>
